<p><b>Jos√© Miguel Cabrera Torres</b> (born April 18, 1983), commonly known as <b>Miguel Cabrera</b> and nicknamed "<b>Miggy</b>", is a <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuelan</a> professional <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> <a href="/wiki/First_baseman" title="First baseman">first baseman</a> who plays for the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB). Since his debut in 2003 he is a two-time¬†<a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL) <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">Most Valuable Player</a> (MVP) award winner, a four-time <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_batting_champions" title="List of Major League Baseball batting champions">AL batting champion</a>, and an eleven-time <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">MLB All-Star</a>. He has played at <a href="/wiki/First_baseman" title="First baseman">first</a> and <a href="/wiki/Third_baseman" title="Third baseman">third base</a> for most of his major league career, but primarily played <a href="/wiki/Left_fielder" title="Left fielder">left</a> and <a href="/wiki/Right_fielder" title="Right fielder">right field</a> before 2006. He claimed the 17th <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown#Batting_Triple_Crown" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">Major League Baseball Triple Crown</a> in 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mlb39371632_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-mlb39371632-1">[1]</a></sup> the first to do so in 45 seasons.</p>
<p>Cabrera was signed in 1999 as an amateur free agent by the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Florida Marlins</a>, and progressed through <a href="/wiki/List_of_Miami_Marlins_minor_league_affiliates" title="List of Miami Marlins minor league affiliates">their minor league system.</a> He made his Major League debut in mid-<a href="/wiki/2003_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2003 Major League Baseball season">2003</a> at the age of 20, and contributed to the Marlins' <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Series" title="2003 World Series">World Series success</a> later that year. Cabrera was a regular player for the Marlins over the next four seasons before being traded to the Detroit Tigers in late 2007. In <a href="/wiki/2012_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2012 Major League Baseball season">2012</a>, Cabrera became the first player since <a href="/wiki/1967_in_baseball" title="1967 in baseball">1967</a> to win the batting <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">Triple Crown</a>, leading the AL with a .330 <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a>, 44 <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home runs</a>, and 139 <a href="/wiki/Run_batted_in" title="Run batted in">RBI</a>, earning him the AL MVP award that year. In¬†<a href="/wiki/2013_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2013 Major League Baseball season">2013</a> Cabrera improved on the previous year's batting performance, including a career-high .348 batting average, and received another AL MVP award.</p>
<p>Cabrera is widely regarded as one of the best pure hitters in baseball and one of the greatest players of his era, combining great <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra_base_hit" title="Extra base hit">power</a> with a high <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a> and good <a href="/wiki/Base_on_balls" title="Base on balls">walk</a> rate, along with a low <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeout</a> percentage. He has hit 30 or more <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home runs</a> during ten separate seasons, driven in over 100 runs in twelve separate seasons (including <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_runs_batted_in_records#Ten_or_more_seasons_with_100_runs_batted_in" title="List of Major League Baseball runs batted in records">eleven consecutive seasons</a>, 2004‚Äì2014), and has a career .321 batting average ‚Äì currently the highest among active players with at least five years of major league service. Cabrera has been praised for hitting many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Line_drive" title="Line drive">line drives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Batted_ball" title="Batted ball">fly balls</a> while maintaining a low <a href="/wiki/Batted_ball" title="Batted ball">pop-up</a> rate, hitting the ball to all fields, and for his notable ability to drive <a href="/wiki/Inside_pitching" title="Inside pitching">inside</a> pitches for home runs.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cabrera was born on April 18, 1983, in <a href="/wiki/Maracay" title="Maracay">Maracay</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aragua_State" title="Aragua State">Aragua State</a>, Venezuela, to parents Miguel and Gregoria (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N%C3%A9e" title="N√©e">n√©e</a> Torres) Cabrera.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_leagues">Minor leagues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Minor leagues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Miguel was signed by the Marlins in 1999 as an amateur free agent<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-2">[2]</a></sup> and came up through their farm system, teaming with future major leaguers <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Gonzalez" title="Adrian Gonzalez">Adrian Gonzalez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dontrelle_Willis" title="Dontrelle Willis">Dontrelle Willis</a>.</p>
<p>He began his professional career in 2000 as a shortstop in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_League" title="Gulf Coast League">Gulf Coast League</a> (GCL). After batting .260 with 10 doubles, two triples and two home runs through 57 games for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GCL_Marlins" title="GCL Marlins">GCL Marlins</a>, Cabrera was promoted to Class-A ball where he finished the final eight games batting .250 with 6 RBIs for the <a href="/wiki/New_York%E2%80%93Penn_League" title="New York‚ÄìPenn League">New York‚ÄìPenn League</a> (NYPL) <a href="/wiki/Utica_Blue_Sox" title="Utica Blue Sox">Blue Sox</a> in <a href="/wiki/Utica,_New_York" title="Utica, New York">Utica, New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref-minors_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-minors-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Heading into <a href="/wiki/2001_in_baseball" title="2001 in baseball">2001</a>, the Marlins bumped Cabrera up to the Low Class-A <a href="/wiki/Kane_County_Cougars" title="Kane County Cougars">Kane County Cougars</a> where he teamed up with current <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> first baseman <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Gonzalez" title="Adrian Gonzalez">Adrian Gonzalez</a>. He earned his way into the <a href="/wiki/All-Star_Futures_Game" title="All-Star Futures Game">Futures Game</a> during All-Star Weekend in Seattle, along with Gonzalez. He ended the year batting .268 with 30 extra-base hits, 66 RBIs, and distinguished himself as having the strongest arm in the <a href="/wiki/Midwest_League" title="Midwest League">Midwest League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Entering the following season, Cabrera was once again promoted, this time to the <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_Hammerheads" title="Jupiter Hammerheads">Jupiter Hammerheads</a> of the High Class-A <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_League" title="Florida State League">Florida State League</a>. At the request of then Marlins coach, <a href="/wiki/Ozzie_Guill%C3%A9n" title="Ozzie Guill√©n">Ozzie Guill√©n</a>, Cabrera made the transition from shortstop to third base. By July, his average was locked in at .277, and he led his team with 45 RBI earning himself a second trip to the Future's game, where he collected two singles. He finished the season batting .278 with 43 doubles and 75 RBIs. Up to this point, he hit just nine homers in his 489 at-bats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>To begin the 2003 season, Cabrera earned another promotion to the Double-A <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Mudcats_(1991%E2%80%932011)" title="Carolina Mudcats (1991‚Äì2011)">Carolina Mudcats</a>. There he teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Dontrelle_Willis" title="Dontrelle Willis">Dontrelle Willis</a>, the left-handed fireballer with whom he would later join in the majors. In his fourth professional season, Miguel was shredding the competition. In April, he hit .402, and by June his average stood at .365 with 10 homers and 59 RBIs before being called up to the majors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_league_career">Major league career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Major league career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_Marlins_.282003.E2.80.932007.29">Florida Marlins (2003‚Äì2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Florida Marlins (2003‚Äì2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2003:_Rookie_year">2003: Rookie year</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2003: Rookie year">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Cabrera made his major league debut on June 20, 2003, at 20 years old; <a href="/wiki/%C3%89dgar_Renter%C3%ADa" title="√âdgar Renter√≠a">√âdgar Renter√≠a</a>, at 19 years old, was the only Marlins player to make his debut at a younger age. Cabrera hit a <a href="/wiki/Walk-off_home_run" title="Walk-off home run">walk-off home run</a> in his first major league game, following <a href="/wiki/Billy_Parker_(baseball)" title="Billy Parker (baseball)">Billy Parker</a> in 1972 and <a href="/wiki/Josh_Bard" title="Josh Bard">Josh Bard</a> in 2002 as the third player since 1900 to hit a game-winning home run in his big-league debut.</p>
<p>Cabrera became the Marlins cleanup batter. Cabrera's postseason play helped propel Florida to a <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Series" title="2003 World Series">World Series</a> championship over the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> and also landed him on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/ESPN_The_Magazine" title="ESPN The Magazine">ESPN The Magazine</a></i> during the offseason.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/National_League_Division_Series" title="National League Division Series">NLDS</a> against the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">Giants</a>, Cabrera hit .286 with three RBIs. After changing positions in the heat of the <a href="/wiki/National_League_Championship_Series" title="National League Championship Series">NLCS</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a>, he hit .333 with three homers and six RBIs.</p>
<p>In game 4 of the <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Series" title="2003 World Series">2003 World Series</a> against the Yankees, Cabrera faced <a href="/wiki/Roger_Clemens" title="Roger Clemens">Roger Clemens</a> for the first time in his career. In the first inning, Clemens threw a 92-mph fastball in the vicinity of Cabrera's chin causing Cabrera to turn and stare at Clemens. Later in the at bat, Cabrera hit a pitch to deep right field for a two-run home run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The home run would give the Marlins an early 2‚Äì0 lead en route to a 4‚Äì3 Marlins victory that evened the series at two games apiece.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Cabrera and the Marlins would go on to win the 2003 World Series in 6 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his first season Cabrera batted .268 (84-for-314), with 12 home runs, 62 RBIs, 39 <a href="/wiki/Run_(baseball)" title="Run (baseball)">runs</a>, 21 <a href="/wiki/Double_(baseball)" title="Double (baseball)">doubles</a>, and three <a href="/wiki/Triple_(baseball)" title="Triple (baseball)">triples</a> in 87 <a href="/wiki/Games_played" title="Games played">games played</a> and received NL <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Rookie_of_the_Month_Award" title="Major League Baseball Rookie of the Month Award">Rookie of the Month</a> honors for both July and September.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2004">2004</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2004">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2004, he batted .294 with 33 home runs, 112 RBIs, 101 runs, 177 hits, a .366 <a href="/wiki/On-base_percentage" title="On-base percentage">on-base percentage</a>, a .512 <a href="/wiki/Slugging_percentage" title="Slugging percentage">slugging percentage</a> from the third and fourth spots in the order, while playing in 160 games and earning his first <a href="/wiki/2004_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2004 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star</a> appearance.</p>
<p>Cabrera spent the entire 2004 season playing in the outfield and had 13 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outfield_assist" title="Outfield assist">outfield assists</a>. In 284 total fielding chances, he committed nine errors (tied for the most among NL outfielders)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> and made 262 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Putouts" title="Putouts">putouts</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2005">2005</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2005">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2005 he was second in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> in hits with 198, and batted .323 with 33 home runs, 43 doubles, two triples, and 116 RBIs. He was voted to his second consecutive All-Star Game along with teammates <a href="/wiki/Paul_Lo_Duca" title="Paul Lo Duca">Paul Lo Duca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dontrelle_Willis" title="Dontrelle Willis">Dontrelle Willis</a>, and won his first <a href="/wiki/Silver_Slugger_Award" title="Silver Slugger Award">Silver Slugger Award</a>. His 33 home runs made him the youngest player in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> history with back-to-back 30 homer seasons, at 22 years, 143 days. <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> did it at 22 years, 223 days. Cabrera also became the first Marlin in history to hit at least 30 home runs and drive in at least 100 runs in back-to-back seasons.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2006">2006</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2006">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Prior to the 2006 season, Cabrera represented <a href="/wiki/Venezuela_national_baseball_team" title="Venezuela national baseball team">Venezuela</a> in the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2006 World Baseball Classic">World Baseball Classic</a>. the Venezuelan team finished seventh in the tournament.</p>
<p>With help from teammates <a href="/wiki/Josh_Willingham" title="Josh Willingham">Josh Willingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dan_Uggla" title="Dan Uggla">Dan Uggla</a> hitting behind and ahead of him respectively, Cabrera finished the year with a .339 batting average, 26 home runs and 114 RBIs. He was selected to his third consecutive All-Star Game and won his second Silver Slugger Award.</p>
<p>On June 22, 2006, pitcher <a href="/wiki/Todd_Williams" title="Todd Williams">Todd Williams</a> let the first pitch of an attempted intentional walk get too close to the plate and Cabrera reached out and singled it to right center field. The hit occurred during 10th inning, scoring the winning run to give the Marlins a 6‚Äì5 lead over the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>During a July 9, 7‚Äì6 road loss to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>, Cabrera became involved in an altercation with teammate <a href="/wiki/Scott_Olsen" title="Scott Olsen">Scott Olsen</a>. With the Marlins trailing 2‚Äì0, Mets catcher <a href="/wiki/Paul_Lo_Duca" title="Paul Lo Duca">Paul Lo Duca</a> hit a hard grounder that glanced off Cabrera's glove and rolled into left field, allowing a run to score as Lo Duca raced to second with a double. As they came off the field, Olsen could be seen shouting something at Cabrera. A moment later, television cameras showed Cabrera in the crowded dugout reaching past teammates to poke his finger at Olsen as the pitcher walked past him. Olsen tried to jab back at Cabrera, who charged Olsen and tried to kick the pitcher before both players were quickly separated by teammates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera was voted to represent the National League All-Stars for the 3rd time in his career and made his first appearance in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Major_League_Baseball_Home_Run_Derby" title="2006 Major League Baseball Home Run Derby">Home Run Derby</a>. Cabrera finished in third place with 15 home runs in the event.</p>
<p>Cabrera battled the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> shortstop <a href="/wiki/Freddy_Sanchez" title="Freddy Sanchez">Freddy Sanchez</a> for the National League batting crown until the last day of the regular season. Marlins manager <a href="/wiki/Joe_Girardi" title="Joe Girardi">Joe Girardi</a> decided to bat Cabrera leadoff for the final game of the season to give him more chances to get a hit for the crown. He ended up finishing second to Sanchez. Cabrera also finished the 2006 campaign with a .568 slugging percentage and a .430 on-base percentage.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MiguelCabrera.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="312" data-file-width="222" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/MiguelCabrera.jpg/170px-MiguelCabrera.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8f/MiguelCabrera.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MiguelCabrera.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cabrera with the <a href="/wiki/2007_Florida_Marlins_season" title="2007 Florida Marlins season">Florida Marlins in 2007</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On February 17, 2007, Cabrera became the first player of the 2007 offseason to win his arbitration hearing, obtaining a one-year contract worth $7.4¬†million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera made his fourth consecutive All-Star game. He was initially scheduled to participate in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Home_Run_Derby" title="Home Run Derby">Home Run Derby</a> during the All-Star weekend, but an injured left shoulder, suffered a few days before the All-Star break, forced him out of the derby and limited him in the All-Star game to a pinch hit at-bat against <a href="/wiki/Dan_Haren" title="Dan Haren">Dan Haren</a> in which he struck out.</p>
<p>On September 4, 2007, Cabrera recorded his 500th RBI as a major leaguer, making him the third-youngest player to accumulate 500 RBIs. Hall of Famers <a href="/wiki/Mel_Ott" title="Mel Ott">Mel Ott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ted_Williams" title="Ted Williams">Ted Williams</a> were the only players to precede him in this feat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fivehundred_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-fivehundred-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 15, 2007, in a game against the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a> at <a href="/wiki/Coors_Field" title="Coors Field">Coors Field</a>, Cabrera drove in at least 100 runs for the fourth consecutive year. His 100th RBI came in the first inning against <a href="/wiki/Ubaldo_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Ubaldo Jim√©nez">Ubaldo Jim√©nez</a>. Five innings later, Cabrera added four more RBIs when he hit a ball 438 feet (134¬†m) into the center field trees for his first career <a href="/wiki/Grand_slam_(baseball)" title="Grand slam (baseball)">grand slam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grandslam_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-grandslam-12">[12]</a></sup> He joined <a href="/wiki/David_Ortiz" title="David Ortiz">David Ortiz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Teixeira" title="Mark Teixeira">Mark Teixeira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Abreu" title="Bobby Abreu">Bobby Abreu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Guerrero" title="Vladimir Guerrero">Vladimir Guerrero</a> as the only players to reach the 100-RBI plateau in each of the four previous seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100-RBI_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-100-RBI-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, Cabrera won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NL_Player_of_the_Week" title="NL Player of the Week">NL Player of the Week</a> twice (April 1‚Äì8 and June 4‚Äì10). He also passed former Marlins <a href="/wiki/Gary_Sheffield" title="Gary Sheffield">Gary Sheffield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Derrek_Lee" title="Derrek Lee">Derrek Lee</a> for second on the franchise home run list. He moved into third in all-time franchise RBIs and first in batting average. Cabrera ended the season with career highs in both home runs and runs batted in.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Detroit_Tigers_.282008.E2.80.93present.29">Detroit Tigers (2008‚Äìpresent)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Detroit Tigers (2008‚Äìpresent)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_on_June_17,_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Miguel_Cabrera_on_June_17%2C_2009.jpg/170px-Miguel_Cabrera_on_June_17%2C_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Miguel_Cabrera_on_June_17%2C_2009.jpg/255px-Miguel_Cabrera_on_June_17%2C_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Miguel_Cabrera_on_June_17%2C_2009.jpg/340px-Miguel_Cabrera_on_June_17%2C_2009.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_on_June_17,_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cabrera in 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On December 5, 2007, the Marlins traded Cabrera and starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Dontrelle_Willis" title="Dontrelle Willis">Dontrelle Willis</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a> for pitchers <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Miller_(baseball)" title="Andrew Miller (baseball)">Andrew Miller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Trahern" title="Dallas Trahern">Dallas Trahern</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eulogio_De_La_Cruz" title="Eulogio De La Cruz">Eulogio De La Cruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burke_Badenhop" title="Burke Badenhop">Burke Badenhop</a>, outfielder <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Maybin" title="Cameron Maybin">Cameron Maybin</a>, and catcher <a href="/wiki/Mike_Rabelo" title="Mike Rabelo">Mike Rabelo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 22, 2008, Cabrera reached an agreement with the Tigers on an eight-year, $152.3 million contract extension. At the time, the deal was the fourth-largest in baseball history, behind those signed by <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jeter" title="Derek Jeter">Derek Jeter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manny_Ramirez" title="Manny Ramirez">Manny Ramirez</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The deal was also the largest in Tigers history at the time, surpassing the five-year, $75¬†million contract signed by <a href="/wiki/Magglio_Ord%C3%B3%C3%B1ez" title="Magglio Ord√≥√±ez">Magglio Ord√≥√±ez</a> in 2005 (it was later surpassed in 2012 when <a href="/wiki/Prince_Fielder" title="Prince Fielder">Prince Fielder</a> signed a 9-year, $214 million deal) Cabrera earned $11.3 million in 2008, and will receive an average of $20 million per year through 2015.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2008">2008</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2008">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Cabrera made his Tigers debut on March 31, 2008, playing third base in a home game against the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>. In his third at-bat, he hit a solo home run off Royals pitcher <a href="/wiki/Gil_Meche" title="Gil Meche">Gil Meche</a>. He finished the game 1-for-5 with two strikeouts, and the Tigers lost 5‚Äì4 in 11 innings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 22, manager <a href="/wiki/Jim_Leyland" title="Jim Leyland">Jim Leyland</a> announced that Cabrera would be moving to first base, with <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Guill%C3%A9n" title="Carlos Guill√©n">Carlos Guill√©n</a> becoming the starting third baseman. Cabrera had already made seven appearances at first, the first appearances at the position of his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera was named the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">AL</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLB_Player_of_the_Month" title="MLB Player of the Month">Player of the Month</a> for July after batting .330 with eight home runs and 31 RBIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 7, Cabrera reached the 1,000-hit plateau on a home run off <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Twins</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Glen_Perkins" title="Glen Perkins">Glen Perkins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera finished the 2008 season with a career-high 37 home runs, which led the American League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> He became the youngest AL home run champion since <a href="/wiki/Troy_Glaus" title="Troy Glaus">Troy Glaus</a> in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> He also established a new career high in RBIs (127).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-2">[2]</a></sup> He became one of only six players who have driven in at least 100 runs in each of the past five seasons, joining Alex Rodriguez, Albert Pujols, <a href="/wiki/David_Ortiz" title="David Ortiz">David Ortiz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Abreu" title="Bobby Abreu">Bobby Abreu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Teixeira" title="Mark Teixeira">Mark Teixeira</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2009">2009</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2009">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Cabrera was selected to play for <a href="/wiki/2009_World_Baseball_Classic_rosters#Venezuela" title="2009 World Baseball Classic rosters">Venezuela</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2009_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2009 World Baseball Classic">2009 World Baseball Classic</a>, along with Tigers teammates <a href="/wiki/Magglio_Ord%C3%B3%C3%B1ez" title="Magglio Ord√≥√±ez">Magglio Ord√≥√±ez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Guill%C3%A9n" title="Carlos Guill√©n">Carlos Guill√©n</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armando_Galarraga" title="Armando Galarraga">Armando Galarraga</a>.</p>
<p>On Opening Day, Cabrera hit a grand slam in left-center that traveled more than 420 feet (130¬†m) at <a href="/wiki/Comerica_Park" title="Comerica Park">Comerica Park</a> to give the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a> a 15‚Äì2 victory over the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a>. Cabrera finished the game 4-for-6 with six RBIs.</p>
<p>On August 23, 2009, Cabrera hit his 200th career home run in his 1,000th career game against the Oakland A's. He became only the fourth Venezuelan player to ever reach that plateau.</p>
<p>Cabrera posted a .324 batting average, which was fourth in the AL. He also tied his career-high in hits with 198, which was also fourth among the AL. He also had yet another 100-plus RBI season making it the sixth straight year for him to reach the 100 RBI mark.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2010">2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_(2011).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2555" data-file-width="2214" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Miguel_Cabrera_%282011%29.jpg/220px-Miguel_Cabrera_%282011%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Miguel_Cabrera_%282011%29.jpg/330px-Miguel_Cabrera_%282011%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Miguel_Cabrera_%282011%29.jpg/440px-Miguel_Cabrera_%282011%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_(2011).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cabrera in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On May 28 in a game against the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> in Detroit, Cabrera hit three home runs in a 5‚Äì4 Tigers loss. Two of the home runs were against starter <a href="/wiki/Ben_Sheets" title="Ben Sheets">Ben Sheets</a>, and one against closer <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bailey_(baseball)" title="Andrew Bailey (baseball)">Andrew Bailey</a>. It was the first three home run game in Cabrera's career, and came in his first game returning to the team after his daughter's birth.</p>
<p>Cabrera was named an AL All-Star for the first time since joining the American League, and the fifth time in his eight-year career. He was chosen to be the starter in place of <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a> star <a href="/wiki/Justin_Morneau" title="Justin Morneau">Justin Morneau</a> who was suffering a <a href="/wiki/Concussion" title="Concussion">concussion</a>. Cabrera also participated in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Major_League_Baseball_Home_Run_Derby" title="2010 Major League Baseball Home Run Derby">Home Run Derby</a>, finishing fourth in the event with 12 home runs.</p>
<p>On September 26 in a game against the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> Cabrera suffered a <a href="/wiki/High_ankle_sprain" title="High ankle sprain">high ankle sprain</a> while getting back to first base on a pick-off attempt. He initially tried to play, but the Tigers decided to shut him down for the remainder of the season. He ended his 2010 season with a .328 batting average, a career-high 38 home runs and 126 RBIs. The lack of a strong #5 hitter to follow Cabrera in the Tigers lineup also resulted in him drawing a career-high 89 walks, which included an AL-leading 32 intentional passes. On defense, he led all AL first basemen in errors, with 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baseball-reference.com_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-baseball-reference.com-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2011">2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_batting_against_Angels_(2012-09-09).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4896" data-file-width="3672" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Miguel_Cabrera_batting_against_Angels_%282012-09-09%29.JPG/170px-Miguel_Cabrera_batting_against_Angels_%282012-09-09%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Miguel_Cabrera_batting_against_Angels_%282012-09-09%29.JPG/255px-Miguel_Cabrera_batting_against_Angels_%282012-09-09%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Miguel_Cabrera_batting_against_Angels_%282012-09-09%29.JPG/340px-Miguel_Cabrera_batting_against_Angels_%282012-09-09%29.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_batting_against_Angels_(2012-09-09).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cabrera batting against the Angels in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cabrera was named to his second AL All-Star team as a reserve, his sixth All-Star Game appearance overall. On July 15, 2011, the first game after the All-Star break, Cabrera collected his 1500th career hit, in a game against the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Cabrera hit for a .344 average, winning the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_Batting_Champions" title="List of Major League Baseball Batting Champions">AL batting title</a>, while also leading the AL in on-base percentage (.448) and doubles (48). He had his eighth straight 100-RBI season (105) and fifth straight 30-HR season (30). He also reached a career-high in walks with 108. On defense, Cabrera led all AL first basemen in errors, with 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baseball-reference.com_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-baseball-reference.com-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera hit .429 with six home runs and 21 RBIs in September 2011, propelling the Tigers into the playoffs and eventually the American League Championship Series. In the first five games of the ALCS, Cabrera had a .565 OBP, as well as a home run and four doubles, one of them off the third base bag.</p>
<p>Through 2011, he had the sixth-best career batting average of all active players (.317), and seventh-best slugging percentage (.555) and OPS (.950).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2012:_Triple_Crown_and_first_MVP_season">2012: Triple Crown and first MVP season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 2012: Triple Crown and first MVP season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/2012_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="2012 Detroit Tigers season">2012</a>, after the signing of first baseman <a href="/wiki/Prince_Fielder" title="Prince Fielder">Prince Fielder</a>, the Tigers announced Cabrera would move back to third base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In a pre-season game with the <a href="/wiki/2012_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2012 Philadelphia Phillies season">Philadelphia Phillies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hunter_Pence" title="Hunter Pence">Hunter Pence</a> batting, Cabrera was struck by a ground ball below the right eye, which broke a bone. Despite this, after seeing the team's <a href="/wiki/Orbit_(anatomy)" title="Orbit (anatomy)">orbital</a> <a href="/wiki/Surgeon" title="Surgeon">surgeon</a>, Dr. Srinivas Iyengar, Cabrera believed he would be ready for opening day on April 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> He was, and was in the starting lineup on Opening Day.</p>
<p>On April 7, he and new teammate <a href="/wiki/Prince_Fielder" title="Prince Fielder">Prince Fielder</a> each hit two home runs against the <a href="/wiki/2012_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2012 Boston Red Sox season">Red Sox</a>, including back-to-back ones in the fifth inning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> That week, from April 4‚Äì8, Cabrera was named AL Player of the Week, his ninth time achieving that honor, five of them being with Detroit. Cabrera hit 5‚Äì11 in three games over that span with three home runs and eight RBI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> On April 27, Cabrera collected his 1,000th RBI in a game against the Yankees. He is one of the few players in league history to reach this plateau before their 30th birthday, joining <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_on_July_13,_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1067" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Miguel_Cabrera_on_July_13%2C_2012.jpg/170px-Miguel_Cabrera_on_July_13%2C_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Miguel_Cabrera_on_July_13%2C_2012.jpg/255px-Miguel_Cabrera_on_July_13%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Miguel_Cabrera_on_July_13%2C_2012.jpg/340px-Miguel_Cabrera_on_July_13%2C_2012.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_on_July_13,_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cabrera during batting practice in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cabrera was named to the American League All-Star team as a reserve, as Rangers third baseman <a href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_Beltr%C3%A9" title="Adri√°n Beltr√©">Adri√°n Beltr√©</a> was voted as a starter. This marked Cabrera's third consecutive All-Star appearance as a member of the Tigers, and seventh appearance overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> On July 22, he hit his 300th career home run off <a href="/wiki/2012_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="2012 Chicago White Sox season">White Sox</a> starter <a href="/wiki/Philip_Humber" title="Philip Humber">Philip Humber</a>. This made Miguel just the second Venezuelan-born player to reach this milestone, joining <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Galarraga" title="Andr√©s Galarraga">Andr√©s Galarraga</a> who hit 399.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 15, Cabrera became the first player in Detroit Tigers history to hit 30 home runs in five consecutive seasons, passing Hank Greenberg (<a href="/wiki/1937_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1937 Detroit Tigers season">1937</a>‚Äì<a href="/wiki/1940_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1940 Detroit Tigers season">40</a>) and Cecil Fielder (<a href="/wiki/1990_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1990 Detroit Tigers season">1990</a>‚Äì<a href="/wiki/1993_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1993 Detroit Tigers season">93</a>), who each had four consecutive 30 home run seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> This also marked the eighth time in the last nine seasons overall that Cabrera has reached the 30 home run mark.</p>
<p>Cabrera was voted the American League Player of the Month for August after batting .357 with six doubles, eight home runs, 24 RBI, 19 runs scored and 12 walks in 26 games. This was the second time that Cabrera was named player of the month for the Tigers as he joined Alan Trammell as the only Tigers to win the award more than once.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Cabrera won the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">Triple Crown</a>, finishing the season with an AL-leading .330 batting average, plus 44 home runs and 139 RBIs which led all of Major League Baseball. He became the first batter to win a Triple Crown since <a href="/wiki/Carl_Yastrzemski" title="Carl Yastrzemski">Carl Yastrzemski</a> in 1967.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Cabrera became the first player to win it without a tie in any of the three categories since <a href="/wiki/Frank_Robinson" title="Frank Robinson">Frank Robinson</a> in 1966. He is the first Latin American player and the first third baseman to win a Triple Crown. Cabrera also had his first career 200-hit season, having hit safely 205 times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> He was named <a href="/wiki/Sporting_News_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="Sporting News Player of the Year Award"><i>The Sporting News</i> Player of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> On October 27, 2012 he was awarded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AL_Hank_Aaron_Award" title="AL Hank Aaron Award">AL Hank Aaron Award</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Cabrera also led the AL in slugging (.606), OPS (.999), total bases (377), and hitting into double plays (28).</p>
<p>In Game 4 of the <a href="/wiki/2012_World_Series" title="2012 World Series">2012 World Series</a>, Cabrera hit his first World Series home run since his rookie year with the Marlins in 2003, putting Detroit on the board for the first time in 2 games. During the bottom of the 10th inning, Cabrera was the final out of the World Series as he struck out looking, completing the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a>' sweep of the Tigers.</p>
<p>On November 15, Cabrera was named the AL's Most Valuable Player over <a href="/wiki/Mike_Trout" title="Mike Trout">Mike Trout</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels" title="Los Angeles Angels">Los Angeles Angels</a>, receiving 22 out of 28 first place votes and 362 points from a panel of Baseball Writers' Association of America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2013:_Second_MVP_season">2013: Second MVP season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2013: Second MVP season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Baseball Hall of Famer</a> <a href="/wiki/Al_Kaline" title="Al Kaline">Al Kaline</a> was quoted in 2013 as saying that Cabrera's performance was "unbelievable", and that Cabrera was already qualified for Cooperstown himself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Bob Nightengale of <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a> Sports called Cabrera "the greatest player in the game of baseball." <a href="/wiki/Barry_Bonds" title="Barry Bonds">Barry Bonds</a> agreed with Nightengale's analysis, adding ""He's the best. By far. Without a doubt. The absolute best.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera continued a torrid pace into the 2013 season, being named <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Player_of_the_Month_Award" title="Major League Baseball Player of the Month Award">American League Player of the Month</a> for May. Cabrera batted .379 (44-for-116) with nine doubles, 12 home runs, 33 RBIs, 23 runs scored and 15 walks in 28 games to claim his third career Player of the Month Award. Cabrera previously won top player honors in July 2008 and August 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The week of August 5‚Äì11, Cabrera was named the American League Co-Player of the Week, with fellow Tigers teammate <a href="/wiki/Austin_Jackson" title="Austin Jackson">Austin Jackson</a>. Cabrera batted .429 (12-for-28) with two doubles, four home runs, 11 RBIs and seven runs scored over seven games, to win his 10th career player of the week award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wk19-2013_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-wk19-2013-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of the 2013 All-Star break, Miguel was hitting .365 with 30 home runs and a league-leading 95 RBIs, considerably better than his 2012 Triple Crown season at the same point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Cabrera became the first player in MLB history to have at least 30 home runs and 90 RBIs before the All-Star break. Cabrera was voted in as the starter at third base for the first time in the fan balloting for the <a href="/wiki/2013_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2013 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2013 Major League All-Star Game</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera won the <a href="/wiki/ESPY_Award" title="ESPY Award">ESPY Award</a> in 2013 for Best MLB Player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> On July 9, 2013, he hit his 350th career home run, against the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a>.</p>
<p>On August 18, Cabrera hit his 40th home run of the season in a game against the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>, joining <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Foxx" title="Jimmie Foxx">Jimmie Foxx</a> as the only MLB players in history to have at least 40 home runs, 120 RBIs and a batting average of .350 or higher through 116 games. Cabrera also became the third Tigers player in history to hit 40 or more home runs in consecutive seasons, joining <a href="/wiki/Hank_Greenberg" title="Hank Greenberg">Hank Greenberg</a> (<a href="/wiki/1937_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1937 Detroit Tigers season">1937</a>‚Äì<a href="/wiki/1938_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1938 Detroit Tigers season">38</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Fielder" title="Cecil Fielder">Cecil Fielder</a> (<a href="/wiki/1990_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1990 Detroit Tigers season">1990</a>‚Äì<a href="/wiki/1991_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1991 Detroit Tigers season">91</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera was named the American League Player of the Month for August. Cabrera batted .356 (36-for-101) with five doubles, 11 home runs, 31 RBIs, 17 runs scored and 13 walks in 27 games to claim his fourth career Player of the Month Award and his second of the <a href="/wiki/2013_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2013 Major League Baseball season">2013 season</a>, after claiming the award in the month of June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the All-Star Break, Cabrera suffered injuries including a groin strain that limited his playing time later in the season. Cabrera finished the regular season with a .348 batting average, and won his third straight <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_batting_champions" title="List of Major League Baseball batting champions">AL batting title</a>. Cabrera became the first Tiger to win three consecutive batting titles since <a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a> (<a href="/wiki/1917_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1917 Detroit Tigers season">1917</a>‚Äì<a href="/wiki/1919_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1919 Detroit Tigers season">1919</a>), and the first American Leaguer to win at least three straight since <a href="/wiki/Wade_Boggs" title="Wade Boggs">Wade Boggs</a> (1985‚Äì88).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> He also led the AL in on-base percentage (.442) and slugging percentage (.636), was second in the league in home runs (44), RBIs (137) and runs scored (103), and was third in walks (90).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 24, Cabrera was honored with his second consecutive <i>Sporting News</i> MLB Player of the Year Award. He is only the fourth player in history to win this award in back-to-back seasons, joining <a href="/wiki/Ted_Williams" title="Ted Williams">Ted Williams</a> (1941‚Äì42), <a href="/wiki/Joe_Morgan" title="Joe Morgan">Joe Morgan</a> (1975‚Äì76) and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> (2008‚Äì09).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 14, Cabrera won his second consecutive <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">American League MVP</a> Award, receiving 23 out of 30 first place votes and 385 points. Cabrera became the first American League player to win back-to-back MVP awards since <a href="/wiki/Frank_Thomas_(designated_hitter)" title="Frank Thomas (designated hitter)">Frank Thomas</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> (<a href="/wiki/1993_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1993 Chicago White Sox season">1993</a>‚Äì<a href="/wiki/1994_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1994 Chicago White Sox season">1994</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> He is only the third Tiger player to win the MVP award more than once, joining <a href="/wiki/Hank_Greenberg" title="Hank Greenberg">Hank Greenberg</a> (<a href="/wiki/1935_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1935 Detroit Tigers season">1935</a>, <a href="/wiki/1940_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1940 Detroit Tigers season">1940</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Hal_Newhouser" title="Hal Newhouser">Hal Newhouser</a> (<a href="/wiki/1944_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1944 Detroit Tigers season">1944</a>‚Äì<a href="/wiki/1945_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1945 Detroit Tigers season">45</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014:_Contract_Extension">2014: Contract Extension</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2014: Contract Extension">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_(15421538951).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1695" data-file-width="923" height="404" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Miguel_Cabrera_%2815421538951%29.jpg/220px-Miguel_Cabrera_%2815421538951%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Miguel_Cabrera_%2815421538951%29.jpg/330px-Miguel_Cabrera_%2815421538951%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Miguel_Cabrera_%2815421538951%29.jpg/440px-Miguel_Cabrera_%2815421538951%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_(15421538951).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cabrera during batting practice in 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1955" data-file-width="1398" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Miguel_Cabrera_2014.jpg/220px-Miguel_Cabrera_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Miguel_Cabrera_2014.jpg/330px-Miguel_Cabrera_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Miguel_Cabrera_2014.jpg/440px-Miguel_Cabrera_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Cabrera_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cabrera in 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the departure of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Fielder" title="Prince Fielder">Prince Fielder</a> via trade, the Tigers announced that Cabrera would return to first base for the 2014 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 28, 2014, the Tigers announced that Cabrera had signed an 8-year contract extension worth $248 million. Combined with the $44 million the Tigers owed on the remaining two years of Miguel's current contract, the total 10-year commitment is worth $292 million. This deal broke the previous record commitment of $275 million the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> tendered to <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a> in 2007. Cabrera's contract has since been surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Giancarlo_Stanton" title="Giancarlo Stanton">Giancarlo Stanton</a>'s 13-year, $325 million contract in 2014, the largest contract in sports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Many analysts criticized the contract as excessive and short-sighted, with <a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a> calling it "the worst." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 4, in a game against the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a>, Cabrera hit a two-run <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home run</a> to notch his 2,000th career <a href="/wiki/Hit_(baseball)" title="Hit (baseball)">hit</a>, becoming the ninth player to reach 2,000 hits before his 31st birthday and the seventh-youngest to reach the mark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 6, it was announced that Cabrera had won the fan voting to start at first base for the American League at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2014 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2014 All-Star Game</a>. This was his ninth All-Star selection overall, and second straight as a starter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In the first inning of the All-Star game, Cabrera hit a 2-run home run off National League starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Adam_Wainwright" title="Adam Wainwright">Adam Wainwright</a>. It was his first career All-Star game home run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera won the ESPY Award for Best MLB Player for a second year in a row in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 7, Cabrera recorded his 100th RBI of the season, reaching the milestone for the 11th consecutive season. Cabrera is only the fifth player in major league history to accomplish this feat, joining <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a> (13 seasons), <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Foxx" title="Jimmie Foxx">Jimmie Foxx</a> (13 seasons), <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a> (13 seasons) and <a href="/wiki/Al_Simmons" title="Al Simmons">Al Simmons</a> (11 seasons).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera was named the AL co-player of the week for the week of September 1‚Äì7. Cabrera batted .500 (15-for-30) with two doubles, five home runs, nine RBI and eight runs scored in seven games to win his 11th career player of the week award. He led the major league in hits, home runs, total bases (32), and slugging percentage (1.067), tied for first overall in runs scored, and tied for second in RBI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera was named the American League Player of the Month for September. Cabrera batted .379 (39-for-103) with 10 doubles, eight home runs, 18 RBI, 39 hits, and 19 runs scored in 26 games to claim his fifth career Player of the Month Award. Cabrera led the league with a .737 slugging percentage and a 1.118 OPS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera finished the regular season with a .313 batting average, 25 home runs, 109 RBI and a league-leading 52 doubles; he led both leagues with 11 sacrifice flies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Along with <a href="/wiki/Matt_Holliday" title="Matt Holliday">Matt Holliday</a> in 2014, Cabrera attained at least 20 HR, 30 doubles, 75 RBI and 80 runs scored each for the ninth consecutive season, becoming just the fourth player in MLB history to do so. The others previously to have accomplished this were <a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial" title="Stan Musial">Stan Musial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manny_Ramirez" title="Manny Ramirez">Manny Ramirez</a>, and Pujols, all with ten consecutive seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 23, Cabrera was announced as a finalist for the American League <a href="/wiki/Rawlings_Gold_Glove_Award" title="Rawlings Gold Glove Award">Gold Glove Award</a> for first base. This marks the first time he was nominated for the accolade. The other two nominees for the award included <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> and the defending Gold Glove winner <a href="/wiki/Eric_Hosmer" title="Eric Hosmer">Eric Hosmer</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> with Hosmer eventually winning the award for 2014 as well.</p>
<p>On October 24, Cabrera underwent surgery to remove a <a href="/wiki/Osteophyte" title="Osteophyte">bone spur</a> in his right ankle that had been bothering him for several months. He also had a procedure to repair a <a href="/wiki/Stress_fracture" title="Stress fracture">stress fracture</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Navicular_bone" title="Navicular bone">navicular bone</a> near the top of his right foot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Doctors knew about the bone spurs, but said the discovery of the broken bone was a surprise. Cabrera himself said he wasn't surprised, stating, "I was feeling a lot of pain. I knew something was wrong." He said he had to alter his swing mechanics the last half of the 2014 season, being unable to put weight on his back foot without pain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2015">2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Cabrera was named the AL player of the week for the week of April 5‚Äì12. Cabrera batted .520 (13-for-25) with two doubles, two home runs, eight RBIs and four runs scored over six Tigers victories to win his 13th career player of the week award. He led the league in total bases (21), hits (13) and on-base percentage (.586), was tied for first in RBIs and was second in batting average and slugging percentage (.840). He finished the week by registering back-to-back four-hit games for the first time in his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 16, 2015, Cabrera hit his 400th career home run against <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Lyons" title="Tyler Lyons">Tyler Lyons</a> of the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a>, making him the all-time leader in home runs among Venezuelan-born players, surpassing the previous record holder, <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Galarraga" title="Andr√©s Galarraga">Andr√©s Galarraga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> At the age of 32 years, 28 days, he is the third-youngest active player to reach this milestone, behind <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> (30 years, 222 days) and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a> (29 years, 316 days), and the eighth-youngest in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 21, Cabrera recorded his 1,400th career RBI. At the age of 32 years, 33 days, he is the fifth-youngest player to reach the milestone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 4, Cabrera was placed on the 15-day disabled list with a Grade 3 left calf strain, including tearing of muscle fibers. This marked the first time Cabrera had been placed on the DL in his 13-year career. At the time of the injury, Cabrera was leading the league in batting average (.350), on-base percentage (.456) and OPS (1.034). He had 16 doubles, 15 home runs and 54 RBIs through 77 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 5, it was announced that Cabrera had won the fan voting to start at first base for the American League at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2015 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2015 All-Star Game</a>, however he was unable to play due to injury. This is the sixth consecutive season that Cabrera has been named an All-Star and the 10th time in his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera was recalled from the disabled list on August 14. On August 16, he recorded his 1,426th career RBI to surpass Andr√©s Galarraga for the most RBIs by a Venezuelan-born player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera finished the 2015 season with a .338 average, 18 home runs, 28 doubles, and 76 RBI. Cabrera's streak of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_runs_batted_in_records#Eight_or_more_consecutive_seasons_with_100_runs_batted_in" title="List of Major League Baseball runs batted in records">eleven consecutive seasons</a> with at least 20 home runs and 100 RBIs was snapped. His .338 batting average led the major leagues, and earned him his fourth AL batting title in the last five years. He is just the seventh player in history to win four AL batting titles, following <a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Heilmann" title="Harry Heilmann">Harry Heilmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wade_Boggs" title="Wade Boggs">Wade Boggs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rod_Carew" title="Rod Carew">Rod Carew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ted_Williams" title="Ted Williams">Ted Williams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nap_Lajoie" title="Nap Lajoie">Nap Lajoie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> He also led the American League with a .440 on-base percentage, and ranked second in the league with a .974 OPS.</p>
<p>Cabrera won his sixth Silver Slugger award, and second at first base, becoming the 18th player to win at least six Silver Slugger Awards. Cabrera joins <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a> as the only players with multiple Silver Slugger Awards at different infield positions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016">2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Cabrera was named the American League Co-Player of the Week, along with fellow Tigers teammate <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Maybin" title="Cameron Maybin">Cameron Maybin</a>, for the week of May 16‚Äì22. Cabrera batted .500/.538/1.000 with three home runs and six RBIs during that time, to win his 14th career player of the week award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> On May 23, Cabrera hit his 500th career double, becoming the 62nd player <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_career_doubles_leaders" title="List of Major League Baseball career doubles leaders">all time</a> to reach the milestone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> On June 12, Cabrera recorded his 2,400th career hit in his 2,000th career game, becoming the fifth-youngest player in MLB history to reach the milestone, at 33 years, 55 days old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 28, Cabrera hit a home run off his former team, the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a>, giving him the distinction of hitting a home run against all 30 Major League teams during his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> On July 5, Cabrera was named to his 11th All-Star team, as a reserve at first base for the American League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> On July 22, Cabrera recorded his 1,500th career RBI, becoming the 56th player in major league history to reach the milestone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Cabrera reached 1,500 RBI with 400+ home runs faster than anyone in Major League history. He is one of six active players with at least 400 home runs and 1,500 RBI, and is more than two years younger than any of the other five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> On August 18, Cabrera recorded his 1,000th RBI as a member of the Detroit Tigers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 5, Cabrera hit his 30th home run of the season and his 300th home run as a Detroit Tiger. He joins <a href="/wiki/Al_Kaline" title="Al Kaline">Al Kaline</a> (399), <a href="/wiki/Norm_Cash" title="Norm Cash">Norm Cash</a> (373) and <a href="/wiki/Hank_Greenberg" title="Hank Greenberg">Hank Greenberg</a> (306) as the only four players to hit 300+ home runs in a Tiger uniform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> On September 18, Cabrera recorded his 2,500th career hit off the Indians' <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Bauer" title="Trevor Bauer">Trevor Bauer</a>, becoming the 100th player in Major League history to reach the milestone, and just the eighth player to do so by his age-33 season. He is the fourth-youngest (33 years, 181 days) to reach 2,500 hits, following <a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera was named the American League Player of the Week for the week of September 26‚ÄìOctober 2. Cabrera batted .565 (13-for-23) with six runs scored, a double, four home runs and 13 RBI over six games. Cabrera finished the period first in hits, RBI, batting average, slugging percentage (1.130) and on-base percentage (.583), second in home runs and total bases (26), and tied for third in runs scored in the American League. This marked Cabrera's 15th weekly honor, tying him with <a href="/wiki/Barry_Bonds" title="Barry Bonds">Barry Bonds</a> for the second-most all-time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Cabrera was named the American League Player of the Month for the period of September 1 to October 2. Cabrera batted .347 (34-for-98) with 20 runs scored, four doubles, 10 home runs and 27 RBI over 26 games to claim his sixth career Player of the Month Award. Among American League leaders in September with a minimum of 80 at-bats, Cabrera finished the month second in slugging percentage (.694), tied for second in home runs and RBI, third in on-base percentage (.443), fourth in batting average, and tied for fourth in hits and runs scored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera finished the 2016 season with a .316 batting average, 38 home runs, 31 doubles, and 108 RBI. He finished tied for first in the AL (with <a href="/wiki/David_Ortiz" title="David Ortiz">David Ortiz</a>) for the most intentional walks (15), and also led the AL by hitting into 26 double-plays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera won the 2016 AL Silver Slugger Award for first basemen, his seventh Silver Slugger Award overall and third award at first base. He is one of 13 Major League players to have won seven or more Silver Slugger awards since the award was introduced in 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_highlights">Awards and highlights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Awards and highlights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cabrera is very active in the community, and in 2012 he began The Miguel Cabrera Foundation to help a variety of children's funds. He also uses his foundation to encourage young kids to play baseball and softball. In 2012 and 2013, Cabrera was nominated by his team for the <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Clemente_Award" title="Roberto Clemente Award">Roberto Clemente Award</a>, honoring the MLB player who best represents baseball on and off the field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera is both a <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> and a practitioner of <a href="/wiki/Santer%C3%ADa" title="Santer√≠a">Santer√≠a</a>. He became a <a href="/wiki/Babalawo" title="Babalawo">babalawo</a> in the 2006 offseason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baxter_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-baxter-95">[95]</a></sup> His wife is named Rosangel, and they have two daughters and one son, born August 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Cabrera and his family live in <a href="/wiki/Birmingham,_Michigan" title="Birmingham, Michigan">Birmingham, Michigan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_matters">Legal matters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Legal matters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the early morning of October 3, 2009, police were called to the Cabreras' home and took Cabrera in for questioning. Cabrera had come home at 6:00am, after a night of drinking at the nearby Townsend Hotel, and got in an argument with his wife. He was seen later that day at a game at <a href="/wiki/Comerica_Park" title="Comerica Park">Comerica Park</a>, with scratches on his face. Cabrera told reporters that the scratches came from his dog and refused to discuss the matter further.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> It was later reported he had a blood alcohol level of .26 when tested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 21, 2010, it was reported that Cabrera spent three months in an alcohol abuse treatment center to help him recover from his addiction. He said at the time he had not consumed any alcohol since he was taken into custody in October 2009, and that he would continue his treatment into spring training and the regular season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cabrera was arrested in Florida on suspicion for drunken driving and resisting arrest on February 16, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was reported that the Tigers' 2012 post-division-clinching celebration held in the clubhouse in Kansas City was not attended by Cabrera, who desired to abstain from the festivities, even though the dousing "champagne" was non-alcoholic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
